ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Loss of Compression:
2. Symptoms: Reduced engine power, excessive exhaust smoke, poor performance [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
3. Troubleshooting: Perform a compression test to determine if there is a loss of compression in cylinders, inspect the piston rings for damage, wear, or improper installation, replace worn or damaged rings with the appropriate size and type [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]

4. Excessive Blow-By:
5. Symptoms: [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
6. (No troubleshooting steps provided in the given context for this symptom)

7. Ring Sticking or Carbon Buildup:
8. Symptoms: Loss of power, poor fuel economy, smoking exhaust [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 304]
9. Troubleshooting: Remove the cylinder head and piston to inspect the rings, examine the rings for carbon buildup or sticking to the piston groove, clean the rings and grooves using an appropriate cleaner and a ring groove cleaning tool, replace any damaged or excessively worn rings [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 304]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Loss of Compression
Symptoms:
• Reduced engine power, excessive exhaust smoke, poor performance [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
Troubleshooting:
• Perform a compression test to determine if there is a loss of compression in cylinders [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
• If compression is low, inspect the piston rings for damage, wear, or improper installation [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
• Replace worn or damaged rings with the appropriate size and type [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]

2. Excessive Blow-By
Symptoms:
• (No symptoms provided) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]
Troubleshooting:
• (No troubleshooting steps provided) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 303]

3. Ring Sticking or Carbon Buildup
Symptoms:
• Loss of power, poor fuel economy, smoking exhaust [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 304]
Troubleshooting:
• Remove the cylinder head and piston to inspect the rings [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 304]
• Examine the rings for carbon buildup or sticking to the piston groove [PDF: scrambler.pdf |

QUERY (original):  what is the general guidlines of coolant refiling

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 317
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 321

  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 320

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Coolant Refilling
• Fill the radiator until coolant escapes at the bleed screw [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Repeatedly squeeze the coolant hoses to expel the air [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Tighten bleed screw [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Top up coolant until the level reaches the top of the filler neck [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Top up expansion tank to the MAX mark [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Engine Coolant Capacity (with reservoir Tank at “Max" Level) – Approximately 1.76 liter [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Install Radiator Cap [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Warm up until opening the thermostat [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Stop the engine and cool down to less than approximately 50°c [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]
• Cool down using external blower to reduce the time [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 321]

Related Sections: Coolant Replacement, Coolant Inspection, Troubleshooting [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 317]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Drain the old coolant from the system [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 194]

2. Flush the radiator with water to remove any remaining coolant and debris [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 194]

3. Refill the system with the recommended coolant mixture [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 194]

4. Bleed the cooling system to remove any air bubbles [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 191]

5. Check the coolant level and top it off as needed to ensure it's within the recommended range [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 318]

6. Dispose of the old coolant properly, following local regulations and guidelines [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 191]

Related Sections: Coolant Inspection, Troubleshooting [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 317]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Coolant Replacement
• Place the vehicle on the paddock [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Position a drip tray beneath the engine [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Remove adaptor plate bolt to drain coolant [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Hold a funnel below the drain and open the radiator cap [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Drain off all the coolant [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Remove fastener, lift out the expansion tank and drain off all coolant [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Install the expansion tank [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Tighten the adaptor bolt along with washer and put vehicle on center stand [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

• Slacken bleed screw in cylinder head [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 320]

Related Sections: Coolant Refilling, Bleeding the Cooling System [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 318]

2. Flush the radiator with water to remove any remaining coolant and debris [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 194]

3. Refill the radiator with the recommended coolant mixture [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 194]

4. Bleed the cooling system to remove any air pockets that may have formed during the refill process [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 318]

  (none / wants_image=False)

  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Place the vehicle on the paddock [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

2. Position a drip tray beneath the engine [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

3. Remove adaptor plate bolt to drain coolant [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

4. Hold a funnel below the drain and open the radiator cap [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

5. Drain off all the coolant [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

6. Remove fastener, lift out the expansion tank and drain off all coolant [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

7. Install the expansion tank [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

8. Tighten the adaptor bolt along with washer and put vehicle on center stand [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

9. Slacken bleed screw in cylinder head [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 320]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Read the DTC from diagnostic tool and take freeze framed data as per diagnostic tool SOP [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]

2. To verify Short to Battery check continuity in between PIN 3 & Pin 5, check continuity in IGN on condition or check continuity between Connector Pin 3 & ECU pin H3 [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]

3. If found any continuity in between PIN 3/ Battery Pin 5: Replace/ Rework wiring harness to resolve issue [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]

4. If not found any issue from Wiring side, then Replace PPTS sensor and start vehicle for 5 min to check if DTC is coming or not [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]

5. When the vehicle is cooled down, then crank the vehicle and accelerate on neutral gear while recording the live data for EWT [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 427]

6. If the EWT value is rising very fast or very slowly and the P1517 fault re-occurs, then the sensor is found NOT OK, replace the EWT sensor with a new one [SOURCE: PDF:

QUERY (original):  explain process to remove fuel pump
QUERY (corrected): explain process to remove fuel pump
wants_image=False  wants_tool=False  wants_steps_with_images=False  has_text_intent=True

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 154
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 155
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 77

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Remove the fuel tank assembly from the vehicle by disconnecting the fuel line supply, canister routing to fuel tank & fuel pump connector, and empty the fuel tank [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]
2. Place the fuel tank sideways on a thick cloth to avoid scratches [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]
3. Disconnect the elbow (Quick fuel Connector) connected to the fuel pump [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]
4. Disconnect the fuel hose connected to the fuel injector, by dislocating the spring clamp [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]
5. Separate the fuel filter and elbow connector from the fuel hose connected to pump and filter by removing both the spring band clamps [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]
6. Remove the fuel pump assembly from the fuel tank assembly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 155]

Related Sections:
• Disassembly of Fuel Filter, Fuel Gauge [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 154]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm level ground [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
2. Front indicator electrical connections can be unplugged from headlamp cowl [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
3. Remove headlamp assembly as mentioned in Headlamp Assembly Section 4.4.5 [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
4. Remove the plastic screw (2) using a T25 Torx socket and take out the grommet (3) to detach the packing plate (1) from headlamp cowl [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
5. Behind packing plate, Unplug the RH & LH side Indicator coupler from main wiring harness, marked in Blue Color for RH Indicator and Orange Color for LH Indicator [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
6. Remove the indicator connector from the back side of the headlamp cowl by cutting the ties securing the connectors [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
7. Remove the M6 screw (2) mounted on the indicator mounting bracket (1) using 5 mm Allen key, Take out collar (4) along with screw (2) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 367]
8. Carefully

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Place the vehicle on paddock on a firmly level ground [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

2. To remove the rear indicators, first remove the rear fender reinforcement from the rear fender assembly to access the rear indicator connectors [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

3. Follow the process mentioned in Section 2.2.4 to remove rear fender re-inforcement [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

4. Disconnect Rear Indicator wiring connection from rear Lamp wiring as shown in fig:
• 1. RH Rear Indicator
• 2. LH Rear Indicator [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

5. Remove the flange nuts (25) and screws (16) to release the rear blinker bracket (36) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

6. Remove both left-hand (LH) and right-hand (RH) turn signal lamps (24) from the "rear fender rear (31)" [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

7. Follow the Reverse procedure to install the rear indicator assembly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368].

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Wiring Harness Main of Top of the Vehicle
• Fuse box is mounted on the frame with a cable tie [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Radiator fan relay is located with a 100 mm relay [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Fuel pump relay has a bracket for mounting [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Roll over sensor is part of the wiring harness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Wiring for the rear lamp is included in the main harness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Auxiliary relay has multiple relays with different lengths: 110 mm, 30 mm, 60 mm, and 50 mm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Diagnostic connector (OBD) is part of the main wiring harness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Battery cable earth junction is connected to the main harness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Earth junction (connector) is also part of the main wiring harness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 378].
• Accessories relay has a bracket for

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Features of the Scrambler
• Telescopic front suspension with 130 mm travel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 38].
• 320 mm dia. front disc with 5mm thickness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 38].
• 255mm dia. rear disc with 5mm thickness [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 38].
• Liquid cooled 344 CC fuel injected engine with co-axial frame and swing arm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 38].
• Neutral Indication (Green Light ON) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• Left Turn Indicator (Green Light Blinks) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• ABS-MIL (Malfunction Indicator light) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• Engine coolant temperature indicator [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• Low Battery Indicator (Red Light ON) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• Single exhaust port with unique upswept exhaust [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].
• Rear shock absorber with 5 step adjustable and 127 mm wheel travel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 40].

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Safety Measures during Swing Arm Assembly Process
• Torque Specifications: Follow the recommended torque specifications provided in the manual when tightening bolts and fasteners. Over-tightening or under tightening can lead to issues with the swing arm's performance and safety. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Alignment: Pay close attention to the alignment of the swing arm. It must be properly aligned with the frame and wheel to ensure stability and safe handling. Use any alignment marks or references provided in the manual. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Secure Bolts: Double-check that all the bolts and fasteners are securely tightened. Use a torque wrench to ensure proper torque levels. Loose bolts can lead to serious accidents. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Check the tightening torque of pivot adjuster, it should be in the specified range. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Check the swing arm visually before assembling it for any cracks /

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Short to Battery Check
• Verify continuity between PIN 3 & Pin 5, or check continuity in IGN on condition or check continuity between Connector Pin 3 & Ecu pin H3. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]
• If found any continuity between PIN 3/ Battery Pin 5: Replace/ Rework wiring harness to resolve issue. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]
• If not found any issue from Wiring side, then Replace PPTS sensor and start vehicle for 5 min to check if DTC is coming or not. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 419]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. TROUBLESHOOTING FOR RH HANDLEBAR & LH HANDLEBAR SWITCH
• Examine the handlebar switch and its wiring for any visible damage, loose connections, or exposed wires [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• Look for any signs of corrosion or rust, which can hinder electrical connections [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• Start by testing each function of the switch (e.g., lights, horn, turn signals) one at a time to determine which, if any, functions are not working [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• If none of the functions work, it could be a power supply or wiring issue [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• Inspect the fuses related to the handlebar switch functions [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• Replace any blown fuses with the correct amperage [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].
• Ensure the relevant relays (if present) are functioning correctly [PDF:scrambler.pdf | Page 362].

    Troubleshooting the headlamp on a BSA motorcycle involves diagnosing and fixing various electrical and mechanical issues.
    i. Wiring Check
        • Inspect the wiring harness for cuts, frays, or loose connections [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]
        • Replace or repair any damaged wiring or connectors [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]
    ii. Fuse Inspection
        • Check the headlamp fuse in the fuse box [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]
        • Replace if blown, using a fuse of the same rating [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]
        • If the new fuse blows immediately, inspect for a short circuit [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]
    iii. Battery Voltage
        • Check the battery voltage [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 365 TYPE: text]

    The replacement procedure of the front indicator involves several steps that need to be followed carefully.
    i. Preparation
        • Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm level ground [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 367]

    ii. Headlamp Assembly Removal
        • Remove headlamp assembly as mentioned in Headlamp Assembly Section 4.4.5 [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 367]
    iii. Packing Plate Removal
        • Remove the plastic screw (2) using a T25 Torx socket and take out the grommet (3) to detach the packing plate (1) from headlamp cowl [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 367]
        • Behind packing plate, Unplug the RH & LH side Indicator coupler from main wiring harness, marked in Blue Color for RH Indicator and Orange Color for LH Indicator [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 367]

            • 2. LH Rear Indicator [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 368]

        • Remove the flange nuts (25) and screws

ANSWER PREVIEW: <b>1.</b> Introduction to Removing the Steering Stem Bolt
        i. The process of removing the steering stem bolt is part of the larger procedure for steering stem removal, which is essential for various maintenance and repair tasks on the motorcycle.
        ii. To access the steering stem bolt, several preliminary steps must be taken to remove other components that obstruct access to the steering stem.
            • The front wheel must be removed, following the procedure outlined in section 2.2.5 [scrambler.pdf | Page 114].
            • The handlebar assembly needs to be removed, referring to section 2.2.9 (A) for the specific steps [scrambler.pdf | Page 114].
            • The fork leg assembly must also be removed from the vehicle, using the guidelines provided in section 2.2.6 (A) [scrambler.pdf | Page 114].
            • With these components removed, access to the steering stem and subsequently the steering stem bolt is facilitated [scrambler.pdf | Page 114].

ANSWER PREVIEW: To disassemble the sub-frame, follow these steps:
1. Remove the Bodywork/Side Panels: Remove the Rear Fender Assembly (Refer Section 2.2.4) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128].
2. Remove the Rear Lighting/Electrics: Disconnect all wiring harness connectors running to the taillight, turn signals, and license plate light. Pull the harness free from any clips or ties on the sub frame [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128].
3. Remove the seat and Seat Latch: Remove the seat and the seat latch, which is secured by screws. Use a Phillips (+) screwdriver to remove the screws [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128].
4. Remove the sub-frame mounting hex bolts (3) & nuts (4) from the main frame using 13 no. socket and 16 no. spanner [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128].
5. Use 6 mm Allen key to remove the socket screws (6) from the frame along with the washers (5) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128].
6. Disconnect the Tail lamp coupler, Cut the cable tie & take out the Sub-frame assembly (2) [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 128]

ANSWER PREVIEW: The points for troubleshooting of the subframe are:
• Visual Inspection: Start with a thorough visual inspection of the frame and sub-frame. Look for signs of damage, rust, cracks, or other abnormalities [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 130].
• Alignment: Check the alignment of the frame and sub-frame. If the frame is not straight, it can lead to handling problems. Ensure that all parts are properly aligned and secured [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 130].
• Rust and Corrosion: Rust and corrosion can weaken the frame over time. If you find any areas with rust, sand it down, apply an anti-rust treatment, and repaint the affected area [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 130].
• Cracks and Welds: Examine all welds for cracks or signs of failure. If you find any, they should be repaired by a professional welder or should be replaced [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 130].

ANSWER PREVIEW: To inspect the side stand, follow these steps:

1. Place the vehicle on a paddock stand firmly on level ground [PDF: scrambler.pdf | Page 136].
2. Locate the side stand, which is mounted on the side of the motorcycle.
3. Visually inspect the side stand for any signs of damage, wear, or corrosion.
4. Check the side stand's mounting points to ensure they are secure and not loose.
5. Check the side stand's pivot point to ensure it is moving freely and not stuck.

Unfortunately, there is no image provided in the context to illustrate the inspection of the side stand. However, the context does provide a table row that describes the side stand ON indicator:

Description: Side stand ON indicator | Function: Displays the text “Side-Stand” in ON condition [PDF: ownerscrambler.pdf | Page 37].

This suggests that the side stand has an indicator that displays when the side stand is in the ON position. During the inspection, you can check the functionality of this indicator to ensure it is working

QUERY (original):  If the drive chain requires any adjustment, the procedure is
QUERY (corrected): If the drive chain requires any adjustment, the procedure is
wants_image=False  wants_tool=False  wants_steps_with_images=False  has_text_intent=True

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 55
  PDF: ownerscrambler.pdf  | Page: 61
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 140
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 54

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Adjustment Procedure**
• Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm, level surface with the transmission in neutral and the ignition switch OFF [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 55]
• Loosen the rear axle nut from RH side using special tool [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 55]
• Turn both drive chain adjustment nuts (1) an equal number of turns until the correct drive chain slack is obtained [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 55]
Alternatively, the steps can also be followed as:
1. Place the motorcycle on a paddock on a firm, level surface with the transmission in neutral and the ignition switch OFF [PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 61]
2. Loosen the rear axle nut from the RH side [PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 61]
3. Turn both drive chain adjusting nuts (1) an equal number of turns until the correct drive chain slack is obtained [PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 61]
 
**Related Sections**
Drive chain inspection and maintenance are discussed in other sections of the manual [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. LH Side and RH Side Panels Removal and Installation Procedure
**Removal Procedure**
• Place the vehicle on Paddock on a firmly level ground / Ramp [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Remove the LH side panel by holding the panel firmly in both hands & pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Follow the same procedure for the RH side panel [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Installation Procedure**
• Follow the Reverse procedure to install the side panels [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Warning**
• Do not apply excessive force or pressure, as this can damage the panels or their mounting points [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• The grommets should remain in place on the vehicle after the panels are removed [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. REMOVAL OF FUEL TANK FROM VEHICLE
**Safety Precautions**
• Before starting, ensure you have the necessary safety equipment.
• Work in a well-ventilated area to avoid inhaling gasoline fumes.
• To prevent electrical accidents, disconnect the negative terminal of the vehicle's battery.
• Take precautions to avoid sparks or open flames while working with gasoline.
**Process**
a. Relieve Fuel Pressure: 
• Locate the fuel pump fuse (EFI Loads) in vehicle and remove it.
• Start the engine and let it run until it stalls. This will depressurize the fuel system.
b. Disconnect the Battery: 
• Disconnect the negative terminal of the vehicle's battery to prevent electrical accidents.
**Tank Mountings Removal**
• The context does not provide the complete steps for tank mountings removal, however it mentions that the fuel tank assembly should be removed from the vehicle by disconnecting the fuel line supply, canister routing to fuel tank & fuel pump connector and emptying the fuel tank [SOURCE: P

• The service life of the drive chain is dependent upon proper lubrication and adjustment [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
• Poor maintenance can cause premature wear or damage to the drive chain and sprockets [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
• The drive chain should be checked, adjusted, and lubricated as part of the periodic inspection [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
• Under severe usage, or when the vehicle is used in unusually dusty or muddy areas, more frequent maintenance will be necessary [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
**INSPECTION**
• Turn the engine off, place the vehicle on paddock & shift the transmission to neutral [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
• Check slack in the lower drive chain run between the sprockets [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
**DRIVE CHAIN NEEDS TO BE INSPECTED FOR**
• Damaged Rollers [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 140]
• Loose Pins [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 14

ANSWER PREVIEW: **FRONT & REAR BRAKE FLUID LEVEL**
• The front brake fluid level should be 1 above the MIN level mark [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 57]
• The rear brake fluid level should be between MIN & MAX [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 57]
• If the level is at or below the MIN level mark, check the brake pads for wear [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 57]
• The recommended brake fluid to be used is DOT 4 (from a sealed container) [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 54]
• The specified brake fluid is DOT4 [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 19]

• Use only non-flammable solvent, not petrol, to clean parts [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 36]

   • Loose or corroded wiring terminals [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 305]
   • Poor ground connection in the electrical system [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 305]
   • Faulty starter motor [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 305]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Troubleshooting of BCM**
• Visual Inspection: Inspect the BCM and its wiring for any obvious physical damage, loose connectors, or corroded terminals. Address any visible issues [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• Battery Voltage Check: Ensure the motorcycle's battery is fully charged and in good condition. Measure the battery voltage with a Multimeter. Low or insufficient voltage can lead to BCM issues (Voltage below 10V) [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• Check Fuse: Inspect the fuses Related to the BCM circuit. Replace any blown fuses or faulty relays [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• BCM Wiring Harness Inspection: Inspect the wiring harness that connects to the BCM. Look for damaged or frayed wires [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Troubleshooting of BCM**
• Visual Inspection: Inspect the BCM and its wiring for any obvious physical damage, loose connectors, or corroded terminals. Address any visible issues [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• Battery Voltage Check: Ensure the motorcycle's battery is fully charged and in good condition. Measure the battery voltage with a Multimeter. Low or insufficient voltage can lead to BCM issues (Voltage below 10V) [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• Check Fuse: Inspect the fuses Related to the BCM circuit. Replace any blown fuses or faulty relays [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].
• BCM Wiring Harness Inspection: Inspect the wiring harness that connects to the BCM. Look for damaged or frayed wires [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 374].

ANSWER PREVIEW: **VALVE CLEARANCE ADJUSTMENT**
1. Refer to the valve clearance specifications: 
   **VALVE CLEARANCE SPECIFICATIONS**
   • Standard: 0.1 ~ 0.15 mm [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 16]
   • Service Limit: - [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 16]
2. Monitor and maintain valve clearances as part of routine maintenance.
3. Check for underlying issues with the valve train, such as worn cam lobes, tappets, or valve seats, if clearances keep changing rapidly.
**IMPORTANT**
• Precision is essential to ensure the engine runs smoothly and efficiently [PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 214]
**WARNING**

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Valve Clearance Adjustment
   **Adjustment Steps**
   • Remove both gauge inspection cover with the help of 4 mm Allen key [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]
   • Use an Allen key of 8mm to turn the [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]
   • Measure the current clearance using a feeler gauge [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]
   • If necessary, the shims may need to be replaced with new ones of the appropriate thickness to achieve the correct valve clearance [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]
   • Once the correct valve clearances are achieved, the engine components are reassembled, and the motorcycle is ready to run smoothly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]
   **Specifications**
   • STANDARD: 0.1 ~ 0.15 mm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 16]
   **Notes**
   • It is essential to follow the BSA guidelines and specifications when adjusting valve clearances [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 210]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Engine Oil Inspection
   **Steps**
   • Place the vehicle on paddock firmly on level surface [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Start the engine and let it idle for 3 - 5 Minutes [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Stop the engine & wait for 2 - 3 minutes [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Remove the dipstick (1) and wipe it clean [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Insert the dipstick until it sits, but do not screw it [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Check the oil levels between the upper and lower-level lines [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • If the level is below the lower-level line (2), remove the oil filler cap (4) and fill the recommended oil up to the upper-level line (3) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Check that the O-rings of the oil filler cap & dipstick are in good condition, replace them if necessary [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 217]
   • Apply engine oil to the O-rings [SOURCE: PDF:scramb

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Engine Oil Replacement
   **Precautions**
   • Engine oil quality is the main factor affecting engine service life [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   • Change the engine oil as specified in the maintenance schedule [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   • When running in dusty conditions, oil changes should be performed more frequently than specified in the maintenance schedule [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   **Engine Oil and Filter Replacement Procedure**
   • Place motorcycle on paddock stand on a firm flat surface [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   • Change the engine oil with the engine at normal operating temperature [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   • Engine oil needs to be drained from two different locations: one is from the engine oil reservoir tank and from the engine sump [SOURCE: PDF:ownerscrambler.pdf | PAGE: 50]
   **Recommended Engine Oil**
   • Refer to the maintenance schedule for the recommended engine oil

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. LH Side and RH Side Panels Removal and Installation Procedure
**Removal Steps**
• Place the vehicle on Paddock on a firmly level ground / Ramp [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Remove the LH side panel by holding the panel firmly in both hands & pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Follow the same procedure for the RH side panel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Additional Removal Steps**
• To remove number board (2), loosen and remove two M5 screws (3) using 3mm Allen key and take out number board (2) from Side Panel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 64]
**Installation Steps**
• Follow the Reverse procedure to install the side panels [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Warning**
• Do not apply

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. LH Side and RH Side Panels Removal and Installation Procedure
**Removal**
• Place the vehicle on Paddock on a firmly level ground / Ramp [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Remove the LH side panel by holding the panel firmly in both hands & pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Follow the same procedure for the RH side panel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• Pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Installation**
• Follow the Reverse procedure to install the side panels [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
**Warning**
• Do not apply excessive force or pressure, as this can damage the panels or their mounting points [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
• The grommets should remain in place on the vehicle after the panels are removed [SOURCE

• Follow the Reverse procedure to install the side panels [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]

• Do not apply excessive force or pressure, as this can damage the panels or their mounting points [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]

• The seat assembly removal procedure is outlined in this section [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 66]

• Remove the seat latch screw [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 22]
• Remove the sub frame socket screw [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 22]

• Refer to page 59 for additional notes on seat assembly removal [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 66]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Battery Charging**
• Ensure the battery is in good condition, as a weak or faulty battery can affect the charging system's performance [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 358]
• Check the battery's terminals for corrosion and ensure they are clean and tight [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 358]
**Charging System Specifications**
• The charging system uses a Three Phase Alternator with a specification of 350w [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 13]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Cylinder Head Installation
   **Installation Steps**
   1. Inspect the cylinder head and related parts for damage, abnormal wear, deformation, burning, or clogs in oil passages [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   2. Replace any part that is out of service limit [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   3. Fit the cylinder head inside 4 hex nuts (Main Studs) [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   4. Apply a thin coat of thread-locking adhesive (Loctite 243) to the threads of each hex nut before fixing [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   5. Fit the head side bolts from the exhaust side (bottom to head) to the cylinder block [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   6. Apply a thin coat of thread-locking adhesive (Loctite 243) to the threads of the bolt before fixing [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   **Specifications**
   • Hex Nut: 4 Nos. - M10 x 1.5 mm [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]
   • Socket Spanner size: 17 mm [SOURCE: PDF:goldstar.pdf | PAGE: 245]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. CYLINDER HEAD INSTALLATION
   **Pre-Installation Checks**
   • Inspect the following parts for damage, abnormal wear, deformation, burning or clogs in oil passages: 
   • Cylinder head
   • Valve springs
   • Valves
   • Valve guides
   • Dowel Pins
   • Replace any part if it is out of service limit [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 245]
   **Installation Steps**
   • Rotate the crank shaft (in Magneto Assembly) to match the TDC marking [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 244]
   • Through the inspection gauge window ensure rotor marking is aligned [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 244]
   • Install the Cylinder Head sub-assembly [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 244]
   • Wipe-off any oil from the journals of the cylinder head, camshaft and camshaft holder [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 244]
   • Fit the Cylinder head inside 4 hex nuts (Main Studs) [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 245]
   • Apply a thin coat of thread-locking adhesive (Loctite 243) to the threads of each hex nut before fixing [PDF: goldstar.pdf | Page 245]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **ENGINE OIL FILTER REPLACEMENT**
• Remove the cap magneto cover (8), by unscrewing the cover bolts (12) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221].
• Pull and take out the Oil filter holder assembly (9) with the oil filter element (11) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221].
• Remove the used oil filter element from the oil filter holder lock [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221].
• Install the new O-ring oil filter (10) and new oil filter (11) into the oil filter holder (9) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221].
• Ensure the oil filter rubber side face must be installed facing towards the engine side [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221].
• Ensure the assembly of oil filter holder and oil filter (Arrow mark) vertically up [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53].
• Use only Genuine oil filter as recommended [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53].
• Ensure the cap magneto cover bolts (12) are tightened securely to the specified torque [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53].

ANSWER PREVIEW: **FUEL LINE / PUMP / FILTER**
1. INTRODUCTION
The major components of fuel system are:
1. Fuel Tank & Fuel lines.
2. Fuel filter.
3. Fuel pump.
4. Fuel sensor / Fuel gauge.
**LOCATION OF PARTS**
• Fuel pump and Fuel gauge are located beneath the fuel tank assembly.
• Fuel Filter is located outside of the fuel tank assembly.
**NOTE**
Before working on the fuel lines, fuel pump and fuel filter all the lines must be empty. No fuel supply should be present in these lines.
For removal of fuel tank assembly follow the procedure mentioned in fuel tank topic of this manual.
[SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 153]

QUERY (original):  how to remove and install spark plug?
QUERY (corrected): how to remove and install spark plug?

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Spark Plug Removal and Installation
**Removal**
• Initially, Remove the spark plug cap by hand [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]
• Use Special tool to remove spark plug, After loosening use spark plug suppressor cap to take it out from cylinder head [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]
**Installation**
• Refit the spark plugs primary & secondary connections are fitted properly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• While replacing hand tight the sparkplug first & tighten it with torque 20 (19-21) Nm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• Do not overtight the Spark plug [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• Ensure that spark plug grade is as per given specification i.e. RA7YC (Champion) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]

   **Introduction**
   • Sub-frame is the extension given to the main frame assembly.
   **Disassembly and Assembly of Sub-frame**
   • Sub-frame in this vehicle is mounted on the rear side of the frame assembly.
   • Sub-frame supports the seat assembly mounting.
   • Sub-frame is made from forging & forming.
   • Main frame assembly and sub-frame are joined by the means of fasteners.
   **Pre-Removal Preparation**
   • Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm level ground.
   • Seat and Seat Latch: Remove the seat and the seat latch, which is secured by screws.
   • Bodywork/Side Panels: Remove the Rear Fender Assembly (Refer Section 2.2.4).
   • Rear Lighting/Electrics: Disconnect all wiring harness connectors running to the taillight, turn signals, and license plate light.
   **Sub Frame Disassembly Procedure**
   1. Remove the sub-frame mounting hex bolts (3) & nuts (4) from the main frame using 13 no. socket and 16 no. spanner [SOURCE: PDF:s

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Safety Measures during Assembly process**
• Torque Specifications: Follow the recommended torque specifications provided in the manual when tightening bolts and fasteners. Over-tightening or under tightening can lead to issues with the swing arm's performance and safety. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Alignment: Pay close attention to the alignment of the swing arm. It must be properly aligned with the frame and wheel to ensure stability and safe handling. Use any alignment marks or references provided in the manual. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Secure Bolts: Double-check that all the bolts and fasteners are securely tightened. Use a torque wrench to ensure proper torque levels. Loose bolts can lead to serious accidents. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **FUEL LINE / PUMP / FILTER**
1. INTRODUCTION
The major components of fuel system are:
1. Fuel Tank & Fuel lines.
2. Fuel filter.
3. Fuel pump.
4. Fuel sensor / Fuel gauge.
**LOCATION OF PARTS**
• Fuel pump and Fuel gauge are located beneath the fuel tank assembly.
• Fuel Filter is located outside of the fuel tank assembly.
**NOTE**
Before working on the fuel lines, fuel pump and fuel filter all the lines must be empty. No fuel supply should be present in these lines.
For removal of fuel tank assembly follow the procedure mentioned in fuel tank topic of this manual [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 153]

QUERY (original):  what is the process for valve clearance?
QUERY (corrected): what is the process for valve clearance?
wants_image=False  wants_tool=False  wants_steps_with_images=False  has_text_intent=True

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 213
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 210
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 213
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 213
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 214
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 212
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 214

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Valve Clearance Setting
   **Adjustment**
   • Follow the same process for all valves.
   • Put the cam in its position & check the TDC mark alignment on sprocket.
   • Put the cam holder, tight all the bolts with 11(9-12) Nm torque & assemble the chain tensioner. Check TDC mark.
   • Check the valve clearance again.
   • If valve clearance is not set properly repeat the same process to adjust the clearance.
   **Measurement**
   • Measure the current clearance using a feeler gauge.
   **Replacement**
   • If necessary, the shims may need to be replaced with new ones of the appropriate thickness to achieve the correct valve clearance.
   **Reassembly**
   • Once the correct valve clearances are achieved, the engine components are reassembled, and the motorcycle is ready to run smoothly.

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. DISASSEMBLY AND ASSEMBLY OF SUB-FRAME
   **Introduction**
   • Sub-frame is the extension given to the main frame assembly.
   • Sub-frame in this vehicle is mounted on the rear side of the frame assembly.
   • Sub-frame supports the seat assembly mounting.
   • Sub-frame is made from forging & forming.
   • Main frame assembly and sub-frame are joined by the means of fasteners.
   **Disassembly and Assembly of Sub-Frame**
   1. **Pre-Removal Preparation**
   • Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm level ground.
   • Seat and Seat Latch: Remove the seat and the seat latch, which is secured by screws. Use a Phillips (+) screwdriver to remove the screws. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 128]
   • Bodywork/Side Panels: Remove the Rear Fender Assembly (Refer Section 2.2.4).
   • Rear Lighting/Electrics: Disconnect all wiring harness connectors running to the taillight, turn signals, and license plate light. Pull the harness free from any clips or ties on the sub frame.
   2. **Sub Fr

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Safety Measures during Assembly process**
• Torque Specifications: Follow the recommended torque specifications provided in the manual when tightening bolts and fasteners. Over-tightening or under tightening can lead to issues with the swing arm's performance and safety. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Alignment: Pay close attention to the alignment of the swing arm. It must be properly aligned with the frame and wheel to ensure stability and safe handling. Use any alignment marks or references provided in the manual. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Secure Bolts: Double-check that all the bolts and fasteners are securely tightened. Use a torque wrench to ensure proper torque levels. Loose bolts can lead to serious accidents. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Check the tightening torque of pivot adjuster, it should be in the specified range. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Spark Plug Removal and Installation
**Removal**
• Initially, Remove the spark plug cap by hand [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• Use Special tool to remove spark plug, After loosening use spark plug suppressor cap to take it out from cylinder head [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
**Installation**
• Clean the insulator tip and electrodes of the plug, carefully using pointed scraper or spark plug cleaner [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• Check the gap between the center and side electrodes with a wire type feeler gauge, Check the gap 0.8 - 0.9 mm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 207]
• Hand tight the spark plug first & tighten it with torque 20(19-21) Nm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]
• Ensure spark plug suppressor cap gets locked properly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]
• Refit the spark plugs primary & secondary connections are fitted properly [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 49]

QUERY (original):  what is the process for valve clearance?
QUERY (corrected): what is the process for valve clearance?

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. Valve Clearance Setting
**Symptoms**
• None
**Process**
• Follow the same process for all valves [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 213]
• Put the cam in its position & check the TDC mark alignment on sprocket 
• Put the cam holder, tight all the bolts with 11(9-12) Nm torque & assemble the chain tensioner [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 213]
• Check TDC mark 
• Check the valve clearance again 
• If valve clearance is not set properly repeat the same process to adjust the clearance [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 213]

**Specifications**
• Inlet Valve : 0.1 to 0.15 mm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 257]
• Exhaust Valve : 0.25 to 0.30 mm [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 257]
**Tool**
• Feeler Gauges [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 257]

**Caution**
• If the valve clearances are not checked and corrected, wear could cause the valves to remain partly open, which lowers performance, burns the valves and valve seats and may cause serious engine damage [SOURCE: PDF:scramble

   • Remove the LH side panel by holding the panel firmly in both hands and pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
   • Follow the same procedure for the RH side panel [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
   • Pull the panel away from the vehicle until it clears the three retaining grommets (leaving the grommets in place) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]
   **Installation**
   • Follow the Reverse procedure to install the side panels [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 63]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Removal of Lower Fender**
• Identify the Lower Fender (11) mounted via the Front Fender Brace (11) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 84]

• Gently remove collars (1) and grommets (10) from lower front fender (11) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 84]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Maintenance Check Points**
• Check the front fork condition by operating the handlebar up and down.
• Check the entire assembly for any leakages & replace front fork oil, if required.
• Check the torque of mounting bolts as per specification.
• Check front fork condition at every service & ensure no accidental damage.
• Per leg fork oil capacity - 390 ml.
• Recommended replacement at 22500 Miles / 36000 kms. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 105]

   **Procedure**

   • Remove the key from the ignition switch [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 110]
   • Remove both LH & RH side mirrors, Rotate RH mirror in anticlockwise direction & LH mirror in clockwise direction [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 110]
   • Before removing the Front Brake Lever Assembly, disconnect the front brake hose from the Front Master Cylinder, which is connected to the ABS unit [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 110]
   • Remove the Banjo Bolt from the Front Master Cylinder [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 110]
   • Carefully detach the Brake Hose from the master cylinder, ensuring the hose is kept at a high level to prevent brake fluid leakage [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 110]

ANSWER PREVIEW: 1. DISASSEMBLY AND ASSEMBLY OF SUB-FRAME
   **PRE-REMOVAL PREPARATION**
   • Place the vehicle on paddock on a firm level ground. 
   • Seat and Seat Latch: Remove the seat and the seat latch, which is secured by screws. Use a Phillips (+) screwdriver to remove the screws. 
   • Bodywork/Side Panels: Remove the Rear Fender Assembly (Refer Section 2.2.4). 
   • Rear Lighting/Electrics: Disconnect all wiring harness connectors running to the taillight, turn signals, and license plate light. Pull the harness free from any clips or ties on the sub frame. 
   **SUB FRAME DISASSEMBLY PROCEDURE**
   1. Remove the sub-frame mounting hex bolts (3) & nuts (4) from the main frame using 13 no. socket and 16 no. [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 128]

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 53
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 272
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 221
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 219
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 96
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 166
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 217
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 220

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Removal of Oil Filter**
• Remove the used oil filter element from the oil filter holder lock [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Pull and take out the Oil filter holder assembly (9) with the oil filter element (11) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Remove the oil filter holder by using plastic rod/handle & ensure no damages to magneto side adapter plate gasket surface [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 272]
**Installation of New Oil Filter**
• Install the new O-ringoil filter (10) and new oil filter (11) into the oil filter holder (9) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221]
• Ensure the oil filter rubber side face must be installed facing towards the engine side [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221] 
• Ensure the assembly of oil filter holder and oil filter (Arrow mark) vertically up [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Use only Genuine oil filter as recommended [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Troubleshooting**
• Visual Inspection: 
  • Start by visually inspecting the swing arm and its components
  • Look for any obvious signs of damage, such as cracks, bends, or missing parts
  • Ensure that all bolts and fasteners are properly tightened [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Lubrication : 
  • Check the swing arm pivot bearings and bushings for proper lubrication
  • Lack of lubrication can lead to excessive wear and play in the swing arm, affecting the bike's handling
  • If necessary, apply recommended lubricant [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Alignment: 
  • Inspect the alignment of the rear wheel
  • An improperly aligned rear wheel can be a sign of swing arm misalignment
  • Use appropriate tools to measure and adjust the alignment if necessary [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 149]
• Swing Arm Bushings and Bearings: 
  • If you suspect problems with the swing arm bushings or bearings, you may need to disassemble the swing arm
  • Inspect these compon

QUERY (original):  What is swing arm troubleshooting?

-- Retrieved Text Chunks --
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 146
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 145
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 148
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 144
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 145
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 144
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 149
  PDF: scrambler.pdf  | Page: 149

-- Image Candidates (all scored) --
  (none / wants_image=False)

-- Final Images Used --
  (none)

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Troubleshooting**
• Visual Inspection: 
  • Start by visually inspecting the swing arm and its components.
  • Look for any obvious signs of damage, such as cracks, bends, or missing parts.
  • Ensure that all bolts and fasteners are properly tightened.
• Lubrication : 
  • Check the swing arm pivot bearings and bushings for proper lubrication.
  • Lack of lubrication can lead to excessive wear and play in the swing arm, affecting the bike's handling.
  • If necessary, apply recommended lubricant.
• Alignment: 
  • Inspect the alignment of the rear wheel.
  • An improperly aligned rear wheel can be a sign of swing arm misalignment.
  • Use appropriate tools to measure and adjust the alignment if necessary.
• Swing Arm Bushings and Bearings: 
  • If you suspect problems with the swing arm bushings or bearings, you may need to disassemble the swing arm.
  • Inspect these components for wear, damage, or excessive play.
  • Replace any worn or damaged parts with new ones.
• Tighten Faste
======================================================================

ANSWER PREVIEW: **Removal of Oil Filter**
• Remove the used oil filter element from the oil filter holder lock [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Pull and take out the Oil filter holder assembly (9) with the oil filter element (11) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Remove the oil filter holder by using plastic rod/handle & ensure no damages to magneto side adapter plate gasket surface [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 272]
• Remove the used oil filter element from the oil filter holder lock [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221] 
**Installation of New Oil Filter**
• Install the new O-ring oil filter (10) and new oil filter (11) into the oil filter holder (9) [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221]
• Ensure the oil filter rubber side face must be installed facing towards the engine side [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 221]
• Ensure the assembly of oil filter holder and oil filter (Arrow mark) vertically up [SOURCE: PDF:scrambler.pdf | PAGE: 53]
• Use only Genuine oil filter as recomme
